# Armor

This article is about the type of apparel. For the magic effect, see [Armor (effect)](Skyrim_Armor_(effect).md). For the spells, see [Armor (spells)](Skyrim_Armor_(spells).md).

**Armor** is a type of apparel that is worn on the body to reduce damage from attacks. Armor comes in two varieties, corresponding to the two different skills governing armor usage: [Heavy Armor](Skyrim_Heavy_Armor.md) and [Light Armor](Skyrim_Light_Armor.md). In addition, there are shields which provide an additional passive increase to armor rating (active blocking is governed by the [Block](Skyrim_Block.md) skill).

Armor comes in several pieces which can be equipped independently of each other. These pieces are:

- **Armor**: covers your legs, chest and shoulders
- **Boots**: covers your feet and ankles
- **Gauntlets**: covers your hands up to your elbow
- **Helmet**: covers your head
- **Shield**: protect and block attacks

The [Divine Crusader](Skyrim_Divine_Crusader.md) [Creation](Skyrim_Creation_Club.md) adds an additional type of armor: the [Fastened Shield of the Crusader](Skyrim_Fastened_Shield_of_the_Crusader.md), which is a **Shoulder** piece.

In addition to standard pieces of armor, two necklaces in the game provide an armor bonus: the [Locket of Saint Jiub](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Locket_of_Saint_Jiub)<sup>[DG](Skyrim_Dawnguard.md)</sup>, and the [Amulet of Articulation](Skyrim_Amulet_of_Articulation.md).

## Armor Materials
Armor appears in several different materials and styles, which determine the quality of the armor. Higher quality armor provides better protection (but is generally heavier). Which quality armor you will find is generally determined based on your character's level.

The following tables describe the *base* level at which an armor type begins to show up randomly for the player. Lower level armor will also randomly appear, but so will higher level armors in certain situations: potentially up to at least 12 levels "early". Enchanted versions of each armor type will begin to appear one level later; see [Generic Magic Apparel](Skyrim_Generic_Magic_Apparel.md) for more information. See [Leveled Lists](Skyrim_Leveled_Lists.md) for details on how these lists are used to determine the probabilities of individual items appearing. Although [Dragonscale](Skyrim_Dragonscale_Armor.md), [Dragonplate](Skyrim_Dragonplate_Armor.md), and [Daedric](Skyrim_Daedric_Armor.md) armors can all be found in random loot, once your level is high enough, the chances of finding any of these armor types is 20 times less than finding other armor types.

Most armor from the list below can be created at [Forges](Skyrim_Forge.md), by using the [Smithing](Skyrim_Smithing.md) skill. The ability to make armor is not dependent upon your character's level, but is instead dependent upon which Smithing perks you have unlocked. All standard armor can also be tempered at [Workbenches](Skyrim_Workbench.md), if you have the necessary auxiliary item. Tempering is twice as effective if you have unlocked the perk necessary to forge that armor. Tempering an enchanted version of the armor (whether custom- [enchanted](Skyrim_Enchanting.md), or [generic](Skyrim_Generic_Magic_Apparel.md)) is similar to tempering the base version - it requires the same auxiliary item, and is twice as effective if you have unlocked the forging perk - but also requires the [Arcane Blacksmith](Skyrim_Arcane_Blacksmith.md) perk to be unlocked.

Jewelry (specifically, [amulets/necklaces](Skyrim_Amulet.md) and [rings](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Ring)), can be created at any blacksmith's forge from ingots and jewels, but these are not counted as protective armor (the two exceptions to this are noted in the section above); similarly, [circlets/crowns](Skyrim_Circlet.md) - like common [clothing](Skyrim_Clothing.md) - have no armor/protection value and cannot be crafted. The [Aetherial Crown](Skyrim_Aetherial_Crown.md), which is a unique, [quest-related](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Lost_to_the_Ages), crafted item (added by the [Dawnguard](Skyrim_Dawnguard.md) add-on), unlike other jewelry items, is eligible for improvement by ordinary [smithing](Skyrim_Smithing.md), but still only ever bears an armor rating of 0.

The [Skyforge](Skyrim_Skyforge.md) allows you to create [Ancient Nord armor](Skyrim_Ancient_Nord_Armor.md), a type of heavy armor, if you finish the [Companions](Skyrim_Companions.md) questline. Also, it may be found from level 1 onward in a few locations. Additionally, there are several other wearable armor sets/pieces that are made available as [loot/specialty gear](Skyrim_Specialty_Gear.md) or as [unique/quest](Skyrim_Unique_Items.md) items; generally, these can all be improved by [smithing](Skyrim_Smithing.md) and possibly fortified with [enchantments](Skyrim_Enchantments.md) (if not enchanted already), though they cannot be forged as player-created items. (*See also:* [Magic Items](Skyrim_Magic_Items.md) and [Artifacts](Skyrim_Artifacts.md))

The [Dragonborn add-on](Skyrim_Dragonborn.md) adds craftable [Bonemold](Skyrim_Bonemold.md) (heavy), [Chitin](Skyrim_Chitin.md) (light/heavy), [Nordic Carved](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Nordic) (heavy), and [Stalhrim](Skyrim_Stalhrim.md) (light/heavy) armors.

The [Dawnguard add-on](Skyrim_Dawnguard.md) adds [2 generic Falmer armors](Skyrim_Falmer_Equipment.md) (heavy) and [Vampire armors](Skyrim_Vampire_Armor.md) (light), which may be worn/improved but cannot be forged by the player.

## Armor Rating
[![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/4/49/SR-graph-Armor_and_Durability.png/200px-SR-graph-Armor_and_Durability.png)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-graph-Armor_and_Durability.png) [](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-graph-Armor_and_Durability.png) Armor Ratios For all of the armor listed on this site, the provided armor ratings are the **base armor ratings**. The actual protection your character will receive from the armor is dependent upon your skill in that armor type and any relevant perks that you have unlocked. The rating can also be improved by using [smithing](Skyrim_Smithing.md) to change the armor's quality to "Fine", "Superior", "Exquisite", "Flawless", "Epic", or "Legendary".

The armor rating only reduces physical damage, not magical damage. Each point of armor rating reduces damage by 0.12%.

**Approximate formulas**:

- *Item Armor rating* = CEILING[ (*base armor rating* + *item quality*) × (1 + 0.4 × (*skill* + *skill effect*)/100) ] × (1 + *unison perk*<sup>†</sup> ) × (1 + *[Matching Set](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Matching_Set)*) × (1 + *armor perk*<sup>‡</sup>)
- *Shield rating* = CEILING[ (*base shield rating* + *item quality*) × (1 + 0.4 × (*skill* + *skill effect*)/100) ] × (1 + *unison perk*<sup>†</sup> ) × (1 + *[Matching Set](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Matching_Set)*)
- *Displayed armor rating* = SUM(*item armor rating*) + *shield rating* + *armor effects*
- *Base damage reduction of 3% per piece worn* = Hidden armor rating of 25 per piece worn, including shields
- *Damage reduction percentage* = *displayed armor rating* × 0.12 + (3.00 × *number of pieces worn).*

† [Custom Fit](Skyrim_Custom_Fit.md) for light armor or [Well Fitted](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Well_Fitted) for heavy armor
‡ [Agile Defender](Skyrim_Agile_Defender.md) for light armor or [Juggernaut](Skyrim_Juggernaut.md) for heavy armor

Clothing and robes do not benefit from the hidden armor rating bonus.

For NPCs the skill coefficient is 1.5 instead of 0.4, and 1.25 ^ 2 (1.5625) instead of 1.25 for Custom Fit.

Note the difference between *skill* effects (e.g. Fortify Light/Heavy Armor equipment, [Ancient Knowledge](Skyrim_Ancient_Knowledge.md)) and *armor* effects (e.g. [Oakflesh](Skyrim_Oakflesh.md), [The Lord Stone](Skyrim_The_Lord_Stone.md)).

Your durability against physical attacks (i.e. the amount of raw damage you can sustain) is proportional to 100/(100 − damage reduction percentage). This results in hyperbolic growth in your physical durability, up to the cap of 80% damage reduction giving a ×5 multiplier to your physical durability. Thus, the more armor rating you have, the more each additional point of armor rating is worth. The graph displayed shows the multiplier to your physical durability relative to no armor based on the displayed armor rating, assuming you are wearing all four pieces of armor (+12% hidden damage reduction) and have no other effects.

### Armor Rating Example
- Dragonscale Armor
- Dragonscale Boots
- Dragonscale Gauntlets
- Dragonscale Helmet
- Dragonscale Shield
- 100 Light Armor Skill
- 100 Smithing Skill (*item quality bonus* of +20 or +10)
- 5/5 [Agile Defender](Skyrim_Agile_Defender.md)
- [Custom Fit](Skyrim_Custom_Fit.md)
- [Matching Set](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Matching_Set)

*Dragonscale Armor rating*

- CEILING [(41 + 20) * (1 + 0.4 * (100/100))] * 1.25 * 1.25 * 2
- = 86 * 1.25 * 1.25 * 2
- = 268.75

*Dragonscale Helmet rating*

- CEILING [ (17 + 10) * (1 + 0.4 * (100/100)) ] * 1.25 * 1.25 * 2
- = 118.75

*Dragonscale Boots rating* & *Dragonscale Gauntlets rating*

- CEILING [ (12 + 10) * (1 + 0.4 * (100/100)) ] * 1.25 * 1.25 * 2
- = 96.875

*Dragonscale Shield rating*

- CEILING [ (29 + 10) * (1 + 0.4 * (100/100)) ] * 1.25 * 1.25
- = 85.9375

*Displayed armor rating*

- 268.75 + 118.75 + 96.875 + 96.875 + 85.9375
- = 667.1875

## Armor Cap
Regardless of your displayed armor rating you can never exceed an 80% physical damage reduction, the **armor cap**. You'll reach the armor cap at 542 displayed armor rating when wearing all four pieces of armor and a shield, 567 without a shield, or 667 when not wearing any armor or shield at all. There are a few different ways you can reach this cap:

**Light / Heavy armor skills only**

Let's say you have 100 armor skill and *all* relevant armor perks acquired and active (i.e. you're wearing a matched set of all light or all heavy armor):

- Without a shield your armor must provide a base armor rating of about 130 (567 / (1.4 * 1.25 * 1.25 * 2)) to reach the armor cap. - *Heavy Armor*: The best heavy armor, [Daedric armor](Skyrim_Daedric.md#Daedric_Armor) has 108 base armor rating → 481 displayed armor rating → 69.8% damage reduction.
- *Light Armor*: The best light armor, [Dragonscale armor](Skyrim_Dragon_Items.md#Dragonscale_Armor) has 82 base armor rating → 362 displayed armor rating → 55.5% damage reduction
- With a shield, you must reach a displayed armor rating of 542 to reach the armor cap. - *Heavy Armor*: Daedric armor with a matching shield yields 560 displayed armor rating, enough to reach the armor cap. The next best Heavy Armor, [Dragonplate](Skyrim_Dragon_Items.md#Dragonplate_Armor) with a matching shield provides 525 displayed armor rating → 78.0% damage reduction
- *Light Armor*: Dragonscale armor with a matching shield yields 426 displayed armor rating → 66.2% damage reduction

**Light / Heavy armor skills + magic effects**

While it's impossible for a light armor user to reach the cap relying only on Light Armor skill and perks, you can still reach the cap without using Smithing, Enchanting, or Alchemy effects. A player with maxed out Light Armor skills, a full set of Dragonscale armor, and a Dragonscale shield will have a displayed armor rating of 423 and a 65.66% damage reduction, 119 less than the 542 displayed armor rating needed to reach the armor cap. Activating the Lord Stone will boost displayed armor rating to 473 and a 71.66% damage reduction. Casting the [armor spells](Skyrim_Armor_(spells).md) Ironflesh or Ebonyflesh will boost displayed armor rating over 542, reaching the 80% armor cap.

**Light / Heavy armor skills + smithing**

Reaching the armor cap becomes significantly easier with smithing. Let's say you have 100 smithing and all relevant smithing perks in addition to 100 armor skill and all relevant armor perks.

- Improving a piece of armor to Legendary quality adds +10 to the armor rating, or +20 if the piece is chest armor. This means that improving a fully matched armor set to legendary boosts the total base armor rating by 20 + 10 + 10 + 10 = 50.
- Without a shield your armor must provide a base armor rating of about 80 to reach the armor cap, since 80 + 50 = 130 (567 / (1.4 * 1.25 * 1.25 * 2)). - *Heavy armor*: A full set of [Chitin](Skyrim_Chitin.md#Chitin_Armor) or [Steel Plate armor](Skyrim_Advanced_Armors.md#Steel_Plate_Armor) provides 87 base armor rating, so any tempered set of heavy armor with equal or greater base armor rating will allow you to reach the armor cap
- *Light armor*: Only Dragonscale armor provides a high enough armor rating (82) to reach the armor cap with tempering
- With a shield, you must reach a displayed armor rating of 542 to reach the armor cap. - *Heavy Armor*: A full set of tempered [Iron Armor](Skyrim_Iron.md#Iron_Armor) with a matching shield yields a displayed armor rating of 547, enough to reach the armor cap. This means that any matching set of heavy armor equal or higher in quality to iron armor can be used to reach the armor cap. Since iron armor is the lowest quality heavy armor, this means that any tempered heavy armor set will reach the armor cap
- *Light armor*: A full set of tempered [Elven Armor](Skyrim_Elven.md#Elven_Armor) with a matching shield yields a displayed armor rating of 550, enough to reach the armor cap. This means that any matching set of light armor equal or higher in quality to elven armor can be used to reach the armor cap.

**Light / Heavy armor skills + smithing + alchemy + enchanting**

With Fortify Smithing enchanted apparel and Fortify Smithing potions you can boost Smithing even further, which can potentially allow *any* material to reach the cap, without needing any further benefits (such as the [Notched Pickaxe](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Notched_Pickaxe)); with maxed out enchanting and alchemy and the appropriate perks, using fortify enchanting potions to make better fortify alchemy apparel to make better fortify enchanting potions, to provide the best available Smithing bonuses, you will add 134 total tempering to any suit *even without a perk*, which is above the 130 rating mentioned above. This means you could temper a theoretical 0-rating suit (which doesn't exist) high enough to hit the cap, and you don't need a shield to get there. *With* a tempering perk, you will nearly double this, adding 259 to any suit you make; this is practically sufficient to drop any non-chest piece from any suit, and even with the loss of *two* armor perks (for wearing a full suit and wearing a matched set), you will still hit the cap, allowing you to walk around without a helmet, if you like - just remember, you will also lose any *other* armor perks you have that trigger from having a piece in all 4 wearable slots.

## Notes
- Clothes such as robes and other apparel do not count as armor, and as such do not benefit from the hidden armor rating bonus.
- [Custom Fit](Skyrim_Custom_Fit.md), [Well Fitted](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Well_Fitted), and [Matching Set](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Matching_Set) perks are applied to shields if the four pieces of worn armor (armor, helmet, gloves, boots) match appropriately. The shield does not have to be of the same set, or even the same type (light or heavy).
- Shields do not benefit from either [Agile Defender](Skyrim_Agile_Defender.md) or [Juggernaut](Skyrim_Juggernaut.md), and do not advance the light or heavy armor skills when struck.
- Armor rating/damage reduction does not affect the speed at which the skill is trained.
- If you drop a piece of armor or clothing in front of an NPC, generally in a city or town, they may run up to you and [ask you](Skyrim_World_Interactions.md#.22Can_I_have_that_armor.3F.22) if you are throwing it away.
- [Guards](Skyrim_Guard_Dialogue.md#Reactions_to_Player.27s_Equipment) may comment on what kind of armor you're wearing, depending on what faction they belong to and what you're wearing at the time.
- With version 1.2.1 of the [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch), the Matching Set perks for Light Armor and Heavy Armor have had their conditions changed so that they're now looking for >= 4 instead of just == 4 to qualify for the perk.

## Creation Club Armor Materials
Same as [Armor Materials](Skyrim_Armor.md#Armor_Materials) (see above for more information) but only the armor added by creation club content.

| 12 | [Elven Hunter](Skyrim_Elven_Hunter_Armor.md)<sup>[CC](Skyrim_Alternative_Armors_-_Elven_Hunter.md)</sup> | [Elven Smithing](Skyrim_Elven_Smithing.md) | [Refined Moonstone](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Refined_Moonstone) | 6 | 51 | 11<sup>[^](#intnote_No_Shield)</sup> | 85<sup>[^](#intnote_No_Shield)</sup> |

[^](#note_No_Shield) Those armors sets have no matching shield so they are given one of the same material, if any available [††](#note_Stahlrim) Forging Stalhrim armor also requires completion of the quest [A New Source of Stalhrim](Skyrim_A_New_Source_of_Stalhrim.md). [†††](#note_Creation_Club) Those sets will be found during their respective quests and then can be forged by the player but will not appear at random in chests or NPCs. [‡](#note_Daedric) All Daedric armor can also be made at the [Atronach Forge](Skyrim_Atronach_Forge.md) (except the boots, see [Atronach Forge bugs](Skyrim_Atronach_Forge.md#Bugs)), in which case the Daedric Smithing perk is not needed, but instead the [Sigil Stone](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim:Sigil_Stone) must be obtained. Tempering armor created at the Atronach Forge is still augmented by the Daedric Smithing perk. [‡‡‡](#note_Daedric_Mail) Daedric Mail set has no helmet.

## Creation Club Light Armor Images
- These images show a male [Nord](Skyrim_Nord.md) in different types of light armor.
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/7/70/SR-item-Leather_Scout_Armor_Male.jpg/200px-SR-item-Leather_Scout_Armor_Male.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-Leather_Scout_Armor_Male.jpg) Leather Scout Armor<sup>[CC](Skyrim_Alternative_Armors_-_Leather.md)</sup> (with hide shield)
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/c/c5/SR-item-Dwarven_Mail_Male.jpg/200px-SR-item-Dwarven_Mail_Male.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-Dwarven_Mail_Male.jpg) Dwarven mail<sup>[CC](Skyrim_Alternative_Armors_-_Dwarven_Mail.md)</sup>
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/4/4a/SR-item-Redoran_Watchman%27s_Helmet_Male.jpg/200px-SR-item-Redoran_Watchman%27s_Helmet_Male.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-Redoran_Watchman%27s_Helmet_Male.jpg) Redoran Watchman's Helmet<sup>[CC](Skyrim_Ghosts_of_the_Tribunal.md)</sup>
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/4/43/SR-item-Remnant_Armor_Male.jpg/200px-SR-item-Remnant_Armor_Male.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-Remnant_Armor_Male.jpg) Remnant Armor<sup>[CC](Skyrim_Redguard_Elite_Armaments.md)</sup>
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/2/2f/SR-item-Dark_Seducer_Armor_Male.jpg/200px-SR-item-Dark_Seducer_Armor_Male.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-Dark_Seducer_Armor_Male.jpg) Dark Seducer Armor<sup>[CC](Skyrim_Saints_%26_Seducers.md)</sup>
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/7/72/SR-item-Netch_Leather_Armor_Male.jpg/200px-SR-item-Netch_Leather_Armor_Male.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-Netch_Leather_Armor_Male.jpg) Netch Leather Armor<sup>[CC](Skyrim_Netch_Leather_Armor.md)</sup>
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/b/b6/SR-item-Shadowed_Netch_Leather_Armor_Male.jpg/200px-SR-item-Shadowed_Netch_Leather_Armor_Male.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-Shadowed_Netch_Leather_Armor_Male.jpg) Shadowed Netch Leather Armor<sup>[CC](Skyrim_Netch_Leather_Armor.md)</sup>
- [![](https://images.uesp.net/thumb/9/9d/SR-item-Boiled_Netch_Leather_Armor_Male.jpg/200px-SR-item-Boiled_Netch_Leather_Armor_Male.jpg)](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/File:SR-item-Boiled_Netch_Leather_Armor_Male.jpg) Boiled Netch Leather Armor<sup>[CC](Skyrim_Netch_Leather_Armor.md)</sup>
